{"nick":"joepie91","message":"store jobs in MySQL, including their 'minimum time' (ie. the timestamp at which they should be placed in the queue); have a single process with an in-memory queue based on promise-task-queue, where the jobs will be placed once their time is hit; use setTimeout to schedule tasks in-memory; make that process track execution and mark a job completed in MySQL once it's done; if the process crashes, then upon restart recover by fetching all the","date":"2018-03-21T11:59:13.700Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"unfinished jobs from MySQL, immediately task-queue-schedule every job that's past its 'minimum time', create new setTimeouts for the rest","date":"2018-03-21T11:59:15.154Z","type":"message"}

{"nick":"floppydh_","date":"2018-03-21T12:00:00.177Z","type":"join"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"key points here are: 1) single central process for job management and distribution and tracking, 2) the only persistent copy of the job list is in MySQL, 3) immediate rescheduling upon restart is to cover the tasks that were already in the in-memory queue when the process crashed, 4) setTimeouts are for scheduling an addition-to-queue for tasks that haven't yet reached their time","date":"2018-03-21T12:00:34.044Z","type":"message"}
